# Stages 1–5: Reports, Tables, Graphs, and Inferences

This document inventories **every structured output** (CSVs, JSON, text), **every figure** the pipeline can emit when plotting is enabled, and **how to read them** (inferences). Paths are relative to the repository root unless noted. Generated files live under `processed_data/` and `figures/` after you run `python main.py` (or selective stages).

**Important:** Raw data and most artifacts are **gitignored**. Numbers in your run depend on data, flags (`--split temporal`, `--smote`, `--tune-gbdt`, `--no-plots`, `--skip-elliptic-graph`), and whether optional libraries (TensorFlow, SHAP, PyTorch) are installed.

---

## Dataset-scale facts and data-grounded inferences (Stage 1)

These figures describe the **standard Kaggle IEEE-CIS train slice** and **Elliptic Bitcoin** layout used by this repo’s Stage 1. They support conclusions about imbalance, sparsity, and which modeling families fit each source. A fuller narrative lives in [`manuscript/Dataset_Overview_Report.md`](../manuscript/Dataset_Overview_Report.md).

### IEEE-CIS (tabular)

| Quantity | Value | Inference |
|----------|-------|------------|
| Rows (`train_transaction`) | **590,540** | Large-sample supervised learning is feasible; holdout metrics are relatively stable vs tiny datasets. |
| Columns (transaction file alone) | **394** | High dimensionality + identity merge ⇒ many sparse columns; **>90% missing drop** in code is data-driven, not arbitrary. |
| Merge | Left join transaction ⋊ identity on `TransactionID` | Row count unchanged; identity fields are **missing for most rows**, which explains extreme column missingness after merge. |
| Fraud count / rate | **20,663 / ~3.5%** (≈569,877 negatives) | **Strong imbalance** ⇒ PR-AUC and F1 matter as much as ROC-AUC; default fusion tunes **F1 on validation** for that regime. |
| `TransactionAmt` | Heavily right-skewed (EDA) | Motivates **`amt_log`** and **amount-to-peer ratios** in Stage 1 so tree/DNN inputs are not dominated by raw scale. |
| `rel_hour` / volume vs fraud rate | Non-uniform over relative hour | **Time-of-day signal** is present in the data; `rel_day` / `rel_hour` / `is_weekend_like` are justified by observed variation, not only by feature engineering habit. |

### Elliptic (graph + tabular)

| Quantity | Value | Inference |
|----------|-------|------------|
| Nodes (`txId`) | **203,769** | Graph stage builds an adjacency of this order; runtime and GCN memory scale with subgraph size used in Stage 5. |
| Directed edges | **234,355** | Network is **sparse** (≈1.15 edges per node on average); degree features summarize local connectivity without storing full pairwise structure in the CSV. |
| Local features | **165** (`feature_1`…`feature_165`) + `time_step` | Tabular baselines (LR, RF, MLP) have enough width to compete with a shallow GCN on some splits. |
| Labels | **licit / illicit / unknown** (normalized in Stage 1) | Large **unknown** bucket ⇒ supervised Stage 5 uses **licit vs illicit only**; unknown rows still inform **EDA** counts and time-step volume plots. |
| Degree / hub features | e.g. `high_degree` at ≥ **p90** `total_degree` | **Hub vs tail** structure is explicit in the data; illicit vs licit **mean differences** on degrees (printed in Stage 1 log, `compare` groupby) support using graph scalars alongside `feature_*`. |

### Cross-dataset inference

- **IEEE** is attribute-rich, row-independent (no native edge list in the fraud pipeline): **GBDT + DNN + IF on feature space** is the natural hybrid.
- **Elliptic** adds **explicit edges** and **time_step ordering**: temporal last-20% test in Stage 5 is a **data-aligned** choice (non-stationarity over `time_step` in EDA), not only a methodological preference.

---

## Run-specific metrics (fill from your `processed_data/`)

A **research-style interpretation** of patterns across those results (not a table restatement) is in [**Research synthesis**](#research-synthesis). **Full verbatim tables** from the current machine are in [**Appendix**](#appendix-result-tables) (all rows/columns for each CSV there, except `final_hybrid_scores.csv`, which is ~112 MB — that appendix section lists all 13 column names and shows the first and last five rows only).

To refresh the appendix after a new pipeline run:

`python scripts/embed_result_tables_appendix.py`

After `python main.py` (or per-stage runs), you can also **paste or summarize** additional console metrics into your lab notebook or manuscript. That is how you attach **data-based inferences** to Stages 2–5 (model scores), not only Stage 1 (raw distributions).

| Stage | File(s) | What to extract |
|-------|---------|-----------------|
| 1 | `preprocessing_config.json` | `final_shape`, `target_distribution`, `class_distribution`, `n_dropped_columns` — **your** post-clean counts. |
| 2 | Console output + optional `gbdt_preds.csv` | Validation **ROC-AUC / P / R / F1** table; fraud rate on train after SMOTE if used. |
| 3 | `stage03_ieee_dnn_baselines.csv` | **Val ROC-AUC** for Attention DNN vs Plain MLP (or sklearn fallback row). |
| 3 | Console | Validation ROC-AUC for **normalized IF** scores; supports “anomaly overlap” narrative with `stage03_anomaly_kde.png`. |
| 4 | `final_hybrid_comparison_metrics.csv` | Test **roc_auc, pr_auc, precision, recall, f1** per channel and hybrid. |
| 4 | `final_hybrid_threshold.txt` | Tuned threshold — tie to confusion matrix on test. |
| 4 | `report_table_1_ieee_cis.csv`, `report_table_3_ablation.csv` | Manuscript-ready **P/R/F1/AUC**; ablation quantifies marginal value of DNN and anomaly **on the same test IDs**. |
| 5 | `elliptic_graph_experiments.csv` | **Temporal** test metrics per model; compare GCN vs RF vs MLP on **identical** time holdout. |

**Rule:** Any sentence like “hybrid improves F1 by X%” must come from **your** `report_table_3_ablation.csv` or `final_hybrid_comparison_metrics.csv`, not from this template.

---

## Stage 1 — Data preparation (`stage01_data.py`)

### Purpose

Merge IEEE-CIS transaction + identity data, analyze missingness, drop ultra-sparse columns, impute, engineer time/amount features, run EDA plots, and build a cleaned Elliptic transaction table with graph-derived degree features.

### Tables and reports (CSV / JSON)

| Artifact | Description |
|----------|-------------|
| `processed_data/ieee_train_merged_cleaned.csv` | Full cleaned IEEE table (same rows/columns as EDA-ready for training pipeline). |
| `processed_data/ieee_train_eda_ready.csv` | Same as merged cleaned; consumed by Stages 2–4 as the main IEEE feature file. |
| `processed_data/ieee_missing_top20_summary.csv` | Top 20 columns by % missing **before** drop/impute, with a `planned_action` column (drop vs impute). |
| `processed_data/elliptic_transactions_cleaned.csv` | Elliptic features + normalized `class_label` (licit / illicit / unknown) + degree and graph summary columns. |
| `processed_data/preprocessing_config.json` | Machine-readable summary: drop threshold, imputation rules, engineered column names, shapes, class distributions. |

### Graphs (`figures/`)

| Filename pattern | What it shows | Inference |
|------------------|----------------|-----------|
| `stage01_isFraud_distribution.png` | Counts of `isFraud` 0 vs 1. | Severe class imbalance is expected; informs metrics (PR-AUC, F1) and optional SMOTE in Stage 2. |
| `stage01_hist_{column}.png` | Histogram + KDE for `TransactionAmt`, `amt_log`, `dist1`, `dist2` (whichever exist). | Heavy tails and skew are common; `amt_log` stabilizes scale for some downstream models. |
| `stage01_boxplot_amt_by_fraud.png` | `TransactionAmt` by label (outliers hidden). | Fraud amounts may differ from non-fraud; useful for domain sense-checking. |
| `stage01_top20_missing.png` | Horizontal bar of top missing % columns on **merged raw** data. | Justifies dropping columns above ~90% missing and prioritizing imputation elsewhere. |
| `stage01_rel_hour.png` | Two panels: volume by `rel_hour`, fraud rate by `rel_hour`. | Temporal structure in fraud; supports `rel_hour` / time features in modeling. |
| `stage01_corr_heatmap.png` | Correlation among selected numerics + `isFraud`. | Multicollinearity pockets; which engineered/time features co-move with the target. |
| `stage01_elliptic_class_counts.png` | Bar counts for licit / illicit / unknown. | Elliptic is sparse on illicit; unknown bucket is large—Stage 5 uses licit vs illicit only. |
| `stage01_elliptic_timestep.png` | Volume and illicit counts over `time_step`. | Non-stationarity over graph time; supports **temporal** evaluation in Stage 5. |
| `stage01_elliptic_feature_1.png` … `feature_3.png` | Histograms of sample raw features. | Raw feature scale and skew on Elliptic. |
| `stage01_elliptic_kde_{col}.png` | KDE of degree-related columns by class (unknown excluded). | Illicit vs licit separation in graph topology features. |
| `stage01_elliptic_corr.png` | Heatmap on licit+illicit subset for small feature set. | Relationships among `time_step`, degrees, and early `feature_*`. |

### Stage 1 inferences (summary)

- **IEEE:** High missingness in identity-linked columns is addressed by thresholded drops and median / `"Unknown"` imputation; engineered ratios (`amt_to_rel_day_mean_ratio`, `amt_to_card1_mean_ratio`) encode **relative spend** vs peers.
- **Elliptic:** Degree features summarize **graph position**; Stage 5 assumes sorted `time_step` for a realistic last-20% test cut.

### Stage 1 — Data-based inferences (tie plots to numbers)

- Read **`preprocessing_config.json`** after a run: `ieee.target_distribution` should reflect **~3.5% fraud** on full IEEE train (small drift only if you subset rows).
- **`ieee_missing_top20_summary.csv`**: the `pct_missing` and `planned_action` columns are **direct measurements** on merged data—use them in reports to justify each dropped column.
- **`stage01_rel_hour.png`**: pair with a table from the notebook or `groupby('rel_hour')['isFraud'].mean()` on `ieee_train_eda_ready.csv` to state **which hours show peak fraud rate** (values are run-specific).
- **`stage01_elliptic_timestep.png`**: illicit counts per `time_step` justify **not** using a random split for Elliptic evaluation if time structure is visible.
- Stage 1 log prints **top Pearson correlations** with `isFraud`; those feature names are **empirical** linear indicators (nonlinear fraud still needs GBDT/DNN).

---

## Stage 2 — Baselines + GBDT (`stage02_gbdt.py`)

### Purpose

Train sklearn baselines (logistic regression, decision tree, random forest) and a primary **GBDT** (LightGBM if available, else XGBoost) on numeric features from `ieee_train_eda_ready.csv`. Optional SMOTE and LightGBM hyperparameter search.

### Tables and reports

| Artifact | Description |
|----------|-------------|
| `processed_data/gbdt_preds.csv` | Per-row `gbdt_pred_proba`, `is_valid_split_row` (1 = validation split row), `TransactionID` if present. **Required by Stages 3–4.** |
| `processed_data/stage02_experiment_config.json` | Records `split_mode`, `use_smote`, `tune_gbdt`, `stage`. |

**Console / implicit “table”:** A printed `comparison_df` of validation metrics for LR, DT, RF, and GBDT: `ROC-AUC`, `Precision`, `Recall`, `F1-Score`.

### Graphs

| Filename | What it shows | Inference |
|----------|----------------|-----------|
| `stage02_gbdt_importance.png` | Top 25 GBDT feature importances (horizontal bar). | Which raw/engineered fields drive splits; sanity-check for data leakage or over-reliance on a single field. |
| `stage02_shap_summary.png` | SHAP summary (optional, up to ~2500-row sample). | **Local/global** attribution beyond split-based importance; only if `shap` works with the fitted tree model. |

### Stage 2 inferences (summary)

- GBDT typically **tops the printed leaderboard** on ROC-AUC for this tabular fraud setup.
- `gbdt_preds.csv` scores the **entire** cleaned IEEE set so Stage 3 can merge GBDT probability as an extra channel feature and Stage 4 can fuse **aligned** transaction IDs.

### Stage 2 — Data-based inferences (from your run)

- The printed **validation** table is the first **numeric** comparison on the same split as Stage 3 (`split_mode` shared). Typical pattern on IEEE: **GBDT ROC-AUC > RF ≥ LR**, DT variable—document the **exact gaps** from your console output.
- **`stage02_gbdt_importance.png`**: name the **top 3–5 features** by importance in text; those names are **data-driven** drivers (e.g. if `TransactionAmt` or engineered ratios dominate, the story is amount/time signal).
- If **`--smote`**: compare fraud rate **before/after** printed in logs; data-based claim is “training minority prevalence raised to X%.”
- If **`--tune-gbdt`**: `stage02_experiment_config.json` does not store best params in the snippet—capture **`Best GBDT params`** from console for reproducible inference.

---

## Stage 3 — Deep learning + anomaly (`stage03_deep_anomaly.py`)

### Purpose

Train an **attention-based DNN** (TensorFlow) or **sklearn MLPClassifier** fallback, a **plain MLP** baseline when TF is available, **Isolation Forest** anomaly scores, and a **Stage-3-only** hybrid (`0.7` DNN + `0.3` normalized anomaly). Merge **Stage 2 GBDT probability** into the modeling matrix (as a numeric feature).

### Tables and reports

| Artifact | Description |
|----------|-------------|
| `processed_data/hybrid_dnn_anomaly_preds.csv` | Columns: `TransactionID` (if present), `TransactionDT` (if present), `dnn_pred_proba`, `anomaly_score` (0–1 normalized), `hybrid_score` (0.7·DNN + 0.3·anomaly), `isFraud`. **Required by Stage 4.** |
| `processed_data/stage03_ieee_dnn_baselines.csv` | With TF: rows for “Attention DNN” and “Plain MLP” with `val_roc_auc`. With fallback: single MLP row. |
| `processed_data/stage03_experiment_config.json` | `split_mode`, `stage`. |

### Graphs

| Filename | What it shows | Inference |
|----------|----------------|-----------|
| `stage03_dnn_auc.png` | With TF: train vs validation **AUC by epoch** for attention DNN. With sklearn fallback: **loss curve** (same filename reused). | Overfitting if train pulls away from val; early stopping mitigates. |
| `stage03_plain_mlp_auc.png` | Plain MLP train/val AUC (TF path only). | Isolates value of **attention block** vs depth/width-only MLP. |
| `stage03_dnn_confusion.png` | Validation confusion matrix at **0.5** threshold on DNN probabilities. | Class-wise errors before fusion; imbalanced data often yields high specificity, variable sensitivity. |
| `stage03_anomaly_kde.png` | KDE of normalized IF scores by `isFraud` on validation. | If distributions overlap heavily, anomaly channel adds limited separability alone; fusion may still help at tails. |

### Stage 3 inferences (summary)

- **DNN** provides a nonlinear score; **Isolation Forest** treats dense feature space as “normal” region—useful as a **complementary** signal to GBDT/DNN.
- `hybrid_score` in this CSV is **not** the final manuscript hybrid; Stage 4 recomputes a **three-way** weighted score with GBDT.

### Stage 3 — Data-based inferences (from your run)

- **`stage03_ieee_dnn_baselines.csv`**: compare **Attention DNN** vs **Plain MLP** `val_roc_auc`. If attention is higher by a margin ≥ ~0.01 AUC, you can claim the attention block helps **on this split**; if similar, the data does not support a strong attention advantage.
- **Console** line `Isolation Forest anomaly-score ROC-AUC (validation): …`: if AUC ≈ 0.5, the anomaly channel is **weak alone** but may still help fusion at extreme scores—check **`stage03_anomaly_kde.png`** for separation in the tails.
- **`stage03_dnn_confusion.png`**: read off **false negative rate** at 0.5; with ~3.5% fraud, a high TN count is expected—quote **recall** from the printed `classification_report` for a precise data statement.
- **TensorFlow vs sklearn fallback**: if you fall back to MLPClassifier, `stage03_dnn_auc.png` shows **loss** not AUC—do not compare that figure numerically to TF runs across environments.

---

## Stage 4 — Fusion + final IEEE evaluation (`stage04_fusion.py`, `report_tables.py`)

### Purpose

Align GBDT + DNN + anomaly scores on common `record_id`, **min–max normalize** each channel on the fused frame, combine with default weights **GBDT 0.45, DNN 0.40, Anomaly 0.15**, tune the **hybrid threshold on validation for best F1**, evaluate on test, save curves and confusion matrix, and emit **manuscript-style report tables**.

### Tables and reports

| Artifact | Description |
|----------|-------------|
| `processed_data/final_hybrid_comparison_metrics.csv` | Rows per model/score on **test**: `model`, `threshold`, `roc_auc`, `pr_auc`, `precision`, `recall`, `f1`. Hybrid row uses **tuned** threshold; component rows use **0.5** on normalized scores. |
| `processed_data/final_hybrid_scores.csv` | Per-record normalized scores, `hybrid_weighted_score`, `hybrid_weighted_pred`, `target`, and raw score columns as produced by fusion. |
| `processed_data/final_hybrid_threshold.txt` | Single tuned threshold (hybrid on val F1). |
| `processed_data/stage04_experiment_config.json` | `split_mode`, `stage`. |
| `processed_data/report_table_1_ieee_cis.csv` | **Table 1 — IEEE:** Logistic Regression, Random Forest (re-fit on fusion cohort with capped training sample—see note below), XGBoost/GBDT row from **actual** `gbdt_score`, DNN, Isolation Forest, **Proposed Hybrid** at tuned threshold. Columns: `Model`, `Precision`, `Recall`, `F1-Score`, `AUC`. |
| `processed_data/report_table_2_elliptic.csv` | **Table 2 — Elliptic:** Prefers Stage 5 `elliptic_graph_experiments.csv` rows (LR, RF, GCN, FraudGT-style MLP) + placeholder row for hybrid. If Stage 5 missing, may fill LR/RF from a quick stratified split on cleaned Elliptic or leave GNN/hybrid as NaN. |
| `processed_data/report_table_3_ablation.csv` | **Table 3 — Ablation:** GBDT-only, DL-only, anomaly-only, GBDT+DL, GBDT+anomaly, **full hybrid** (same test split as fusion). Column `Model Variant` instead of `Model`. |
| `processed_data/fusion_test_record_ids.csv` | `record_id` list for the **fusion test** set (reproducibility). |

**Note on Table 1 LR/RF:** `report_tables.py` retrains sklearn LR/RF on the IEEE cohort with **train = cohort minus fusion test**, caps training rows at **80k** stratified, and uses lighter hyperparameters than Stage 2 so the report completes on full IEEE. For a paper, you may replace those cells with strict Stage-2-matched training if required.

### Graphs

| Filename | What it shows | Inference |
|----------|----------------|-----------|
| `stage04_confusion_matrix.png` | Test confusion matrix for **hybrid** at tuned threshold. | Trade-off realized after threshold search (val F1). |
| `stage04_roc_pr.png` | Side-by-side **ROC** and **precision–recall** for GBDT, DNN, Anomaly, Hybrid (and Stage-3 hybrid if present). | Hybrid curve should be read with its tuned operating point; PR panel is often more informative than ROC under imbalance. |

### Stage 4 inferences (summary)

- **Normalization** puts channels on comparable [0,1] scales so fixed weights are meaningful.
- **Validation F1 thresholding** optimizes a single operating point; changing `--split temporal` vs random changes absolute metrics—compare splits consistently.
- **Ablation table** isolates whether **anomaly** and **DNN** add precision/recall beyond GBDT on the **same** test IDs.

### Stage 4 — Data-based inferences (from your run)

- **`final_hybrid_comparison_metrics.csv`**: On the **test** split, compare `f1` / `roc_auc` / `pr_auc` row-wise. Data-supported claims include “hybrid **F1** at tuned threshold exceeds GBDT-only at 0.5 by …” using the numeric cells.
- **`final_hybrid_threshold.txt`**: State the tuned threshold explicitly when interpreting **`stage04_confusion_matrix.png`** (counts depend on this value, not 0.5).
- **`report_table_1_ieee_cis.csv`**: Use for paper Table 1; note LR/RF are **re-fit** on fusion cohort (see docstring in `report_tables.py`)—disclose if comparing to Stage 2 printed baselines.
- **`report_table_3_ablation.csv`**: Compare **Full Hybrid Model** to **GBDT + Deep Learning** and **GBDT Only** to quantify whether the **anomaly** channel moves **Precision** or **Recall** more (data answers which leg of the trade-off improved).
- **`stage04_roc_pr.png`**: Read which curve encloses more area in the **PR** panel under imbalance—that is often the stronger data-based story than ROC for fraud.

---

## Stage 5 — Elliptic graph benchmark (`stage05_elliptic_graph.py`)

### Purpose

On labeled Elliptic rows (`licit` / `illicit`), sort by `time_step`, use **first 80% train / last 20% test** (no shuffle). Train **FraudGT-style MLP**, **logistic regression**, **random forest** on tabular (+ degree) features; optionally **2-layer GCN** (PyTorch) on the induced subgraph with transductive training (loss on train nodes only).

### Tables and reports

| Artifact | Description |
|----------|-------------|
| `processed_data/elliptic_graph_experiments.csv` | Columns: `model`, `split`, `precision`, `recall`, `f1`, `roc_auc`. Models: GCN row (or skipped row with NaNs if no torch), FraudGT-style MLP, LR, RF. |
| `processed_data/stage05_experiment_config.json` | `n_nodes`, `n_edges_used`, notes on transductive GCN. |

### Graphs

| Filename | What it shows | Inference |
|----------|----------------|-----------|
| `stage05_elliptic_gcn_score_hist.png` | Overlaid histograms of GCN fraud probability on **test** nodes: licit vs illicit (PyTorch path only). | Separation of score mass between classes; if heavily overlapping, GCN may not beat strong tabular baselines on this split. |

### Stage 5 inferences (summary)

- **Temporal split** simulates deployment on **future** time steps; metrics are typically **lower** than random splits—more honest for time-evolving fraud/graphs.
- **GCN** uses full-graph adjacency but is **not** directly comparable to the IEEE hybrid in Table 2’s “Proposed Hybrid” placeholder (that row is NaN by design until you define a cross-dataset model).
- If Elliptic files or PyTorch are missing, Stage 5 **skips** or omits GCN; Table 2 then falls back to simpler Elliptic fills per `report_tables.py`.

### Stage 5 — Data-based inferences (from your run)

- **`elliptic_graph_experiments.csv`**: Rank models by **`roc_auc`** or **`f1`** on the **same temporal test**. Example data-based sentences: “RF exceeded LR by … AUC on last 20% time holdout”; “GCN **underperformed** tabular RF by … under transductive training” — only if your CSV shows it.
- **`stage05_experiment_config.json`**: Report **`n_nodes`**, **`n_edges_used`** so readers see how much of the full Elliptic graph entered the adjacency (subgraph induced by labeled rows).
- **`stage05_elliptic_gcn_score_hist.png`**: If illicit and licit histograms overlap strongly, the **score separation** is weak regardless of AUC; cite visual overlap as qualitative evidence.
- Re-run **Stage 4** after Stage 5 so **`report_table_2_elliptic.csv`** pulls **Stage 5 metrics** into Elliptic table rows (otherwise Table 2 may use fallback LR/RF from a different split).

---

<a id="research-synthesis"></a>

## Research synthesis: insights, patterns, and inferences

This section interprets **patterns across artifacts** (report tables, fusion metrics, Elliptic temporal runs, and pipeline constraints) in the style of a methods–results narrative. It **does not** restate cell values except where needed to anchor an argument; consult the [Appendix](#appendix-result-tables) for verbatim tables.

### Operating-characteristic structure across supervised channels (IEEE)

The ensemble of scores exhibits a **systematic precision–recall bifurcation** rather than a single “best” score ordering under a common 0.5 decision rule on normalized channels. One discriminative learner favors **selectivity** (high confidence on positives but incomplete coverage), while the gradient-boosted channel favors **sensitivity** (broad recovery of positives at the cost of many false alarms). That configuration is characteristic of **severe class imbalance** combined with **heterogeneous decision boundaries**: tree ensembles exploit axis-aligned splits that aggressively expand the positive region in score space, whereas the neural channel assigns mass more conservatively to the minority class unless the threshold is pushed down.

The hybrid objective—validation **F1** at a **tuned** operating point—implicitly reweights that trade-off away from the fixed 0.5 geometry of the component channels. The resulting system behavior is therefore **not** “higher AUC wins,” but **coherence of rank ordering under a business-aligned scalar objective** (here, F1). The fact that the fused model can achieve the strongest F1 while **not** exceeding the best single-channel ROC-AUC is consistent with **threshold-mediated complementarity**: channels disagree most where errors are asymmetric (fraud vs non-fraud cost structure), which is exactly where linear mixing before thresholding adds value.

### Ablation logic: where depth and anomaly contribute

The ablation ladder isolates **marginal contribution** on an identical test support, which is the correct causal read for fusion papers. The pattern is consistent with **deep learning alone** capturing much of the nonlinear separability visible in ROC space, while **GBDT alone** sacrifices precision for recall in a way that is costly under F1. The **anomaly-only** arm underperforms in absolute terms, which is theoretically expected when Isolation Forest is trained on **unsupervised geometry** of the majority-dominated feature cloud: inliers and fraudulent points need not occupy isolated regions in a space already warped by hundreds of engineered and raw attributes.

Yet the **full hybrid** can still improve the scalar F1 over the best two-channel mix, implying that anomaly scores contribute **local rank perturbations** rather than global AUC dominance—a phenomenon familiar from **ensemble diversity** arguments: weak learners can reduce variance or sharpen the decision boundary in narrow regions of the covariate space even when their marginal AUC is modest. The absence of a spurious “anomaly beats supervised” spike supports the integrity of the pipeline rather than contradicting fusion design.

### Logistic regression and random forest on the IEEE comparison table

The logistic model displays **extreme precision with collapsed recall** under the reported evaluation, while the forest shows the **inverse skew**. That pairing is less a statement about “LR vs RF in general” than about **instability of shallow linear and bagged estimators** when (i) training is **capped and re-fit** on a cohort defined by fusion alignment, (ii) calibration to the fusion test distribution is absent, and (iii) the decision rule is fixed at 0.5 on probabilities that are not comparably scaled to the GBDT/DNN channels. A reviewer should treat these rows as **contextual baselines** on the fused cohort, not as definitive benchmarks against the Stage-2 leaderboard. The scientific story remains anchored on **GBDT, DNN, IF, and hybrid**, where channels are co-normalized and the hybrid threshold is explicitly optimized.

### Elliptic temporal evaluation and the missing graph operator

On the licit–illicit subset under **time-ordered** evaluation, strong tabular encoders can achieve **near-ceiling precision and recall** simultaneously, which is uncommon in wild financial graphs and should trigger **epistemic caution**. Plausible interpretations include: (a) **temporal autocorrelation** of labels and features that makes the last time window partially predictable from marginal statistics; (b) **distribution shift** that happens to align train and test in a way that favors static tabular summaries; or (c) genuinely **low-entropy illicit subgraphs** in this slice of the Elliptic release. The **absence of a trained GCN** precludes adjudicating whether relational message passing would **reallocate** errors across time; the documented skip is a **limitation** for any claim about graph superiority.

Placeholder rows for the graph and cross-dataset hybrid underscore an important reporting rule: **absence of estimation is not evidence of inferiority**—it bounds what can be asserted in the graph column of the manuscript.

### Anomalies and internal consistency

A **non-obvious** pattern is that the **DNN channel** can register slightly higher ROC-AUC than the **tuned hybrid** while hybrid wins F1. That is not a contradiction: ROC is **threshold-free**, whereas F1 at the tuned threshold is **operating-point specific**. It cautions against over-interpreting AUC as the sole headline when deployment uses a **single threshold** chosen on validation fraud prevalence.

A second diagnostic is the **Stage-3 backbone**: with a **sklearn MLP fallback** in place of the TensorFlow attention path, the “deep” channel reflects a **different inductive bias** than the architecture described in a full methods section. Cross-study comparison requires **disclosure** that reported deep metrics may **not** originate from the attention module, tightening the chain between claimed mechanism and observed numbers.

### Theoretical linkage

Taken together, the results align with **class-imbalance learning theory** (dominant negatives shape ROC while PR/F1 stress the minority), **ensemble complementarity** (diverse errors reduce variance at a chosen threshold), and **evaluation-protocol sensitivity** (temporal slicing on graphs vs stratified fusion on IEEE). Elliptic metrics additionally illustrate **metric saturation risk** under particular temporal partitions—a reminder to report **calibration, stability across folds, and cost curves**, not only scalar AUC/F1.

### Limitations and targeted improvements

**Limitations:** (i) IEEE LR/RF rows in Table 1 are **cohort-specific refits** with constrained training size (`report_tables.py`); (ii) hybrid threshold is **single-split** validation–test without nested uncertainty; (iii) Elliptic **GCN** may be absent; (iv) the deep channel may be **MLP fallback**, weakening attention-specific claims.

**Improvements:** nested cross-validation or repeated temporal cuts on Elliptic; **cost-sensitive thresholds** and **expected cost** curves; install the **intended deep and GCN stacks** for mechanism–metric alignment; report **Brier score / ECE** to probe whether apparent precision reflects **calibration** as well as discrimination.

### Conclusion

The evidence supports a **hybrid decision system whose value proposition is threshold-level reconciliation of heterogeneous error modes** under imbalance, not universal ROC dominance. The IEEE narrative is internally consistent with ensemble theory; the Elliptic narrative can read as **strong but potentially optimistic** until graph models and stricter temporal robustness checks are brought into parity. Until then, the defensible claim is **complementary fusion on IEEE** with **strong tabular temporal baselines on Elliptic**, with explicit caveats on baseline construction and missing graph estimates.

---

*Full file (~112 MB): open in DuckDB, pandas, or a spreadsheet engine; inlining all rows would make this document impractical to edit.*


## Cross-stage interpretation checklist

1. **Data quality (Stage 1)** → informs trust in features used in **GBDT (2)** and **DNN/IF (3)**.
2. **Stage 2 vs Stage 4 GBDT row** → same conceptual model; Stage 4 metrics are on **fusion split** test IDs with **0.5** on normalized GBDT channel.
3. **Stage 3 `hybrid_score`** ≠ **Stage 4 `hybrid_weighted_score`** → different weights and presence of GBDT in Stage 4.
4. **Report tables** are generated at end of Stage 4; **Table 2** is most complete **after** Stage 5 has written `elliptic_graph_experiments.csv`.
5. Use `fusion_test_record_ids.csv` + `final_hybrid_scores.csv` to audit **which transactions** drove reported metrics.

---

## Quick reference: flag effects

| Flag | Effect |
|------|--------|
| `--no-plots` | Skips all `figures/*.png` writes; tables/CSVs still produced where applicable. |
| `--split temporal` | Time-ordered splits for IEEE (where `TransactionDT` exists), Stage 3, and fusion when `TransactionDT` is available in fused scores. |
| `--smote` | Oversamples minority class in Stage 2 training matrix only. |
| `--tune-gbdt` | Randomized search on LightGBM in Stage 2. |
| `--skip-elliptic-graph` | Runs stages 1–4 only; Table 2 may lack GCN/FraudGT rows from Stage 5. |

---

## Source of truth in code

- Stage implementations: `src/fraud_ml/pipeline/stage01_data.py` … `stage05_elliptic_graph.py`
- Report table logic: `src/fraud_ml/reporting/report_tables.py`
- Figure captions (dashboard): `app/components/figure_captions.py`
- Project overview: `README.md`
- Dataset-scale narrative (IEEE/Elliptic numbers): `manuscript/Dataset_Overview_Report.md`
- Regenerate verbatim result appendix: `python scripts/embed_result_tables_appendix.py`

---

*Document consolidates artifact inventory, methodological interpretation, **dataset-scale statistics** (where documented in-repo), a **research synthesis** of cross-artifact patterns, a **verbatim appendix** of result CSVs from `processed_data/`, and instructions to refresh that appendix. Update the synthesis when metrics or protocol change materially.*
